If just skip the filter, the codes after the loop will be called with\n693:     // wrong data. For encodeData, the response_encoder->encode() will be called.\n694:     if ((*entry)->end_stream_) {\n695:       return;\n696:     }\n697:     ASSERT(!(state_.filter_call_state_ & I've completed the code review of the Envoy HTTP filter chain PR. Here's a summary of the defects found:\n\n## Review Summary\n\nI've identified **5 defects** in the PR and documented them in `/workspace/review.json`:\n\n### Critical Defect\n1. **header_utility.cc (line 41)** - `matchHeaders()` logic inverted: When no header match criteria are configured (empty config), the function returns true (match all), which is backwards. If a filter specifies no headers to match, it should apply to NO requests, not ALL requests. This breaks the fault filter's header-based injection logic.\n\n### High Severity Defects\n2. **fault_filter.cc (line 170)** - Lambda captures `request_headers` by reference in a timer callback. While currently safe due to stream lifetime guarantees, this is a dangerous pattern that could cause use-after-free if code is refactored.
